<span id="freeTextContainer6078624884994871454">When a down-on-her-luck divorcee meets a determined-to-dominate detective, they find out that falling in love can be murder...<br />Nell Dysart's in trouble. Weighed down by an inexplicable divorce and a loss of appetite for everything, Nell is sleepwalking through life until her best friend finagles a job for her with a shabby little detective agency that has lots of potential</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText6078624884994871454">When a down-on-her-luck divorcee meets a determined-to-dominate detective, they find out that falling in love can be murder...<br />Nell Dysart's in trouble. Weighed down by an inexplicable divorce and a loss of appetite for everything, Nell is sleepwalking through life until her best friend finagles a job for her with a shabby little detective agency that has lots of potential and a boss who looks easy to manage.<p><br />Gabe McKenna isn't doing too well, either. His detective agency is wasting time on a blackmail case, his partner has decided he hates watching cheating spouses for money, and his ex-wife has just dumped him...again. The only thing that's going his way is that his new secretary looks efficient, boring, and biddable.<br />But looks can be deceiving and soon Nell and Gabe are squaring off over embezzlement, business cards, vandalism, dog-napping, blackmail, Chinese food, unprofessional sex, and really ugly office furniture, all of which turn out to be the least of their problems. Because soon, somebody starts killing people. And shortly after that, they start falling in love...</p></span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_537888435">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/537888435" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/45618-karen" class="left imgcol" title="karen"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1451916298p2/45618.jpg" alt="karen" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/537888435?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Feb 13, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/45618-karen" class="user" title="karen">karen</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/33728.Fast_Women" title="Paperback 9780312932794" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/45618-karen?shelf=for-that-bodice-ripper-group" class="actionLinkLite">for-that-bodice-ripper-group</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer537888435">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5421810587239096041">yeah, i'm surprised, myself. but it's a different kind of four-star rating. because while there were elements i thought were unsuccessful and dippy characters whose actions confused me, you don't sit down and eat a tub of frosting with a wooden spoon and then complain about the aftertaste.<br /><br />i just don't usually have this much <em>fun</em> with the titles for the bodice rippers society. they are fine, but usually they are trying too hard to be sexxy, which is a total turn-off. <br /><br /><img class="escapedImg" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380409929i/803124.jpg" /><br /><br />this one was goofier, and i th</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText5421810587239096041">yeah, i'm surprised, myself. but it's a different kind of four-star rating. because while there were elements i thought were unsuccessful and dippy characters whose actions confused me, you don't sit down and eat a tub of frosting with a wooden spoon and then complain about the aftertaste.<br /><br />i just don't usually have this much <em>fun</em> with the titles for the bodice rippers society. they are fine, but usually they are trying too hard to be sexxy, which is a total turn-off. <br /><br /><img class="escapedImg" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380409929i/803124.jpg" /><br /><br />this one was goofier, and i think i responded to that, being that way inclined myself.<br /><br />not that i am anything like any of the ladies in this book. i am not myself a headstrong woman who is attracted to a headstrong man and who considers an argument to be foreplay. i am not a young, bosomy blonde in a happy marriage to a considerably older man when i suddenly realize i am not, in fact, happy through the discovery of china egg cups with feet: <br /><br /><span>[image error]</span><br /><br /><img class="escapedImg" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380409929i/803126._SX540_.jpg" /><br /><br /><img class="escapedImg" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380409929i/803127.jpg" /><br /><br /><img class="escapedImg" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380409929i/803128.jpg" /><br /><br /><img class="escapedImg" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380409929i/803129._SX540_.jpg" /><br /><br />nor am i a drunk mystic or whatever-the-h margie was supposed to be.<br /><br />this is what i imagine <em>sex in the city</em> was like, but with more murders and more noir set-pieces.it is a bunch of ladies sitting around talking frankly about vibrators and men, and their relationship problems, without admitting their own failures in these relationships. willful blindness FTW!!<br /><br />because the women here aren't helpless victims to big bad unfeeling men. nell frequently oversteps her bounds in her new job as secretary of a detective firm - breaking shit, dog-napping, snooping and cleaning and forcing her interior design ideas on a man who has no interest in change. suze gets all bent out of shape over <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span style="display: none" class="spoilerContainer">[ her husband's infidelity <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, seeming to forget that she secured this relationship <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span style="display: none" class="spoilerContainer">[by sleeping with a married 40-year-old man when she was 18. in a cheerleader's outfit. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> which, ew. margie is a kooky alcoholic who never really seems all there, but will drop bombshells every once in a while. drunk waters run deep and all. her relationship issues are the least of her problems, actually. and yet, considered in the sober light of day, they are the most explosive.<br /><br />this book operates in a world without consequences (okay, people get murdered, so there are <em>some</em> consequences for some people...) but here, a woman can <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span style="display: none" class="spoilerContainer">[make out with her best friend who is, frankly, a little off-putting in her "i have suddenly become bi-curious, and you are going to have to put up with my repeated advances" <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> with no shyness the next day. and here, a woman can <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span style="display: none" class="spoilerContainer">[ have a one-night stand with the cousin/business partner of her intended with no lasting repercussions to her job or her relationship. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> which, trust me, in the real world, these things have consequences. awkward, long-lasting consequences. you can't un-see someone's genitals.<br /><br />but again, this is frivolous fun, and it would be childish to elevate it and hold it to real-world realities. <br /><br />it is simply a light genre-blend of mystery and romance which is genuinely funny in places.<br /><br />and this is the moral i took from this story:<br /><br /><img class="escapedImg" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380409929i/803130.jpg" /><br /><br /><em>Tobias: You know, Lindsay, as a therapist, I have advised... a number of couples to explore an open relationship where the couple remains emotionally committed but free to explore extramarital encounters.<br /><br />Lindsay: Well, did it work for those people?<br /><br />Tobias: No, it never does. I mean, these people somehow delude themselves into thinking it might, but... but it might work for us.</em> <br /><br />where you substitute "open relationship" for "sleeping with the boss."<br /><br />NOT AT ALL PAINFUL!<br />jennifer crusie, who knew???<!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="5421810587239096041">...more</a>

    <div class="section">
      

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_558718771">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/558718771" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/131922-mark-monday" class="left imgcol" title="mark monday"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1446402303p2/131922.jpg" alt="mark monday" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/558718771?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Mar 20, 2013</a>

      <a href="/user/show/131922-mark-monday" class="user" title="mark monday">mark monday</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/33728.Fast_Women" title="Paperback 9780312932794" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to mark by: </span>
      RBRS (Assignment #6)
  </div>



          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/131922-mark-monday?shelf=romantika" class="actionLinkLite">romantika</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer558718771">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1218123953503233199">my first contemporary (and heterosexual) romance. or in this case, a "romantic mystery". cute, fun, and even ocasionally interesting. the situations and attitudes depicted in this novel are so outside of my experience that at times i felt like i was reading a scifi novel. which was not a bad feeling. <br /><br /><em> <a href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/523760555">do you live in a bubble?</a> </em> <br />interesting question. my first instinct is to say No, of course i don't. that's probably everyone's first instinct; who wants to live in a bubble, who wants to admit that?</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText1218123953503233199">my first contemporary (and heterosexual) romance. or in this case, a "romantic mystery". cute, fun, and even ocasionally interesting. the situations and attitudes depicted in this novel are so outside of my experience that at times i felt like i was reading a scifi novel. which was not a bad feeling. <br /><br /><em>
  <a href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/523760555">do you live in a bubble?</a>
</em> <br />interesting question. my first instinct is to say No, of course i don't. that's probably everyone's first instinct; who wants to live in a bubble, who wants to admit that? my friends are a nice diverse mix, racially and culturally and economically and in amount of education, type of work, even sexual orientation i suppose (hi, i'm the queer one!) i come from a working class background. i live in a big city. my work allows me to meet and get to know all sorts of people from all sorts of backgrounds. etc, etc. and yet while reading this i felt like i must live in some kind of bubble because this novel seems to rather blithely assume that the personal and romantic situations and entanglements on display are all familiar, normal even. but nope, not to me.<br /><br /><em>
  <a href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/541439334">so did the ladies of the novel feel like aliens to you?</a>
</em> <br />well i guess they sorta did. at least in their central situations and in the issues that were the most important to them. i don't know women my age who find their men by being their assistants or secretaries, who assume that a cute boss is a potential romantic interest, who have work lives that seem to regularly integrate work with playing the romantic field. i'm not talking about random hook-ups with co-workers; who hasn't had that, that's a part of life. but i don't really have any peers who define their lives by the men in their lives or whose romantic lives can be jump-started by the potential of romance at work. all that felt strange to me. not off-putting, just odd and rather off-kilter. is this how it is for a lot of women? or a lot of women of a particular socio-economic status, in a particular place and time in america or similar countries? i dunno. and the relationship to money also felt off-kilter to me. when i think of my older female relatives, the ones who may be most like the women in this novel, i think of independent women but i also think of women who are utterly financially dependent on their husbands. that just didn't seem like a serious factor to the women in this novel. so rather strange and rather alien to me, yes. but it wasn't strange in an off-putting way. it was fascinating! is this how <em>normal</em> people think and act? perhaps i should take Fast Women as a way to understand the normals.<br /><br /><em>
  <a href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/189215146">did this feel like a real "romance", one with real people who make real mistakes and none of that bullshit that seems so typical in supposedly romantic fantasy scenarios?</a>
</em> <br />yes it did! as foreign as the situations felt to me, the actual personalities of the four central characters (look, matching sets) were all rather wonderfully real. i loved the give and take in the central relationships. our heroine's thought processes felt nuanced and realistic and full of understandable errors in judgment and many moments of surprising empathy and many moments of the kind of cluelessness with which i'm all too familiar. i really appreciated the protagonist. maybe because she is an older woman, maybe because she is portrayed as attractive but recognizably flawed, maybe because she is a critical, well-meaning control freak Virgo like myself. i responded to her and came to truly understand her. i liked her. i liked all four of them. the banter and the arguments and the give-and-take between the two couples were - sorry to repeat myself - both out of some foreign land that i've never visited AND enjoyable in how there were no doormats involved. everyone gives as good as they get. no one throws themselves at anyone's feet in the moony, irritating way i've seen in various romantic YA or PNR novels. everyone is an adult who makes mistakes. refreshing!<br /><br /><em>
  <a href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/537888435">have you ever made out with your friends? and isn't that weird?? and how about any serious repercussions to a one-night stand with a colleague?</a>
</em><br />- well, yes to the first question. <br />- no, not really, to the second. maybe i have less - ahem - uptight people in my social circles.<br />- and no to the third as well. maybe some awkwardness but hey that's life.<br />so when i came across those instances in the novel, i actually found them all to be thoroughly familiar and so those bits felt pleasantly real to me. they were some of the less alien moments in Fast Women. i'm glad they were included because they made the world of the novel feel more grounded in the kind of slowly but surely shifting of relationships that happen all the time between people of the real world. at least the real world that i know and live in.<br /><br /><em>
  <a href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/25111197">Does Crusie urge readers to conceive of love as a process of mutual understanding and giving, to which honesty -- most of all with oneself -- is indispensable?</a>
</em><br />well yes, she sure does. well said, Miriam.<br /><br />so in sum, i liked this pleasing little entertainment. an interesting window into a certain kind of world, likeable characters, and with a central message that i fully support. plus i learned a lot about different sorts of china. <br /><br />nice one, Crusie.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="1218123953503233199">...more</a>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_357357048">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/357357048" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/5309539-exina" class="left imgcol" title="Exina"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1442497118p2/5309539.jpg" alt="Exina" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/357357048?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jun 11, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/5309539-exina" class="user" title="Exina">Exina</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/33728.Fast_Women" title="Paperback 9780312932794" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/5309539-exina?shelf=favorites" class="actionLinkLite">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer357357048">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6500775070392704506"><blockquote> <strong> <em>“This does not sound like lust.” <br />“Thank God.” <br />“This sounds like luv.”</em> </strong> </blockquote><br /><em>Fast Women</em> is an entertaining contemporary mystery romance. It is about a group of people, who in some sense are all connected to each other. These connections are so complicated that I had to write a list of the characters for myself.<br /><br />The main characters are Nell and Gabe. Gabe is devilish and tempting, Nell is “gracefully efficient” and go-ahead. Nell enters Gabe’s life, and she rearranges not only his office, but his whol</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText6500775070392704506"><blockquote>
  <strong>
    <em>“This does not sound like lust.” <br />“Thank God.” <br />“This sounds like luv.”</em>
  </strong>
</blockquote><br /><em>Fast Women</em> is an entertaining contemporary mystery romance. It is about a group of people, who in some sense are all connected to each other. These connections are so complicated that I had to write a list of the characters for myself.<br /><br />The main characters are Nell and Gabe. Gabe is devilish and tempting, Nell is “gracefully efficient” and go-ahead. Nell enters Gabe’s life, and she rearranges not only his office, but his whole life, future, and helps to solve a mystery stuck in the past.<br /><br />I loved it! Loved Nell and Gabe, Suze and Riley, Chloe, Margie, and Marlene!<br />I loved it because this book is filled with comic situations, spirited characters, witty and lively dialogues, and so many emotions!<br />Riley, oh, he is soooo hot… I prefer Riley to Gabe… And there are such colorful secondary characters, Suze, Margie, Jase, Chloe, Lu, Linney, Becca the “Check-Out Girl”, Jack, …oh, too many…<br /><br /><img class="escapedImg" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380382212r/739945._SX540_SY540_.jpg" /><br /><br />The story is exaggerated and real at the same time.<br />Exaggerated, because it is packed with main and subplots, a mystery plot, secondary and tertiary characters, divorces, and lots of wives, murders, blackmailing, investigations, power-fights, quarrels, and secrets. The story also features important issues, such as friendship, family, love versus lust, marriage, adultery, faith, reputation. <br /><br />Real, because it indicates that life is never black or white. You can be insecure, confident, you decide something, then you can change your mind. You may want something, but don’t know how to get it, or don’t dare to get it, or simply don’t know exactly what you want. It also could happen that you just don’t realize that you want it. Sometimes you are just chatting about crazy things, sometimes serious issues. You may keep things in secret, or blab something important out unintentionally. You make mistakes, you can be hurt, then you forgive. Or take revenge.<br /><br />Relationships and connections are complicated, even without murders and blackmailing. The mystery plot adds extra excitement to the story, but <em>Fast Women</em> is a very enthralling novel even without it.<br />The story takes several months, and at the end, not everything is settled, but hopefully heading in positive direction. <br /><br />There is only one thing I was disturbed by and I would be glad if it was omitted: the love relationship of Nell’s son Jase and Gabe’s daughter Lu. I felt it forced and hasty, because they are very young, and it is so weird that their parents are in love with each other too.<br /><br /><a rel="nofollow" href="http://exinasreadings.com/contemporary-romance/fast-women/">Originally posted on my blog on July 11, 2012.</a><br /><a rel="nofollow" href="http://exinaart.tumblr.com/tagged/Fast-Women">My favorite quotes.</a></span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_189215146">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/189215146" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/94602-kelly" class="left imgcol" title="Kelly"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1437154881p2/94602.jpg" alt="Kelly" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/189215146?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jul 26, 2011</a>

      <a href="/user/show/94602-kelly" class="user" title="Kelly">Kelly</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/33728.Fast_Women" title="Paperback 9780312932794" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/94602-kelly?shelf=fiction" class="actionLinkLite">fiction</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/94602-kelly?shelf=romantical" class="actionLinkLite">romantical</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/94602-kelly?shelf=wits-and-fools" class="actionLinkLite">wits-and-fools</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/94602-kelly?shelf=21st-century" class="actionLinkLite">21st-century</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/94602-kelly?shelf=grande-dames" class="actionLinkLite">grande-dames</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/94602-kelly?shelf=mawwiageiswhatbringsustogethertoday" class="actionLinkLite">mawwiageiswhatbringsustogethertoday</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer189215146">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12199910453251991719">ALERT, ALERT, ALERT! I think I found one! A real romance novel that feels like a romance novel! It negated most of the problems I have with romance novels: that the people I'm supposed to like are assholes, that it all happens too fast and unrealistically, that the main characters spend all their time thinking about each others crazy crazy amazing bodies. And and and! Women's sexuality isn't fetishized as pure as the driven snow. Possessiveness happens, sure, but you know, when it's realistic. N</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText12199910453251991719">ALERT, ALERT, ALERT! I think I found one! A real romance novel that feels like a romance novel! It negated most of the problems I have with romance novels: that the people I'm supposed to like are assholes, that it all happens too fast and unrealistically, that the main characters spend all their time thinking about each others crazy crazy amazing bodies. And and and! Women's sexuality isn't fetishized as pure as the driven snow. Possessiveness happens, sure, but you know, when it's realistic. Not every relationship is dramatized to the utmost. Women can make a lot of mistakes, and as long as they are still smart, strong and sexy, all is well. AS IT SHOULD BE. Adults often talk to each other like adults, things take months to develop, there's realistic conflict of feelings and interests, the supporting characters have their own story lines and problems (which are also engaging, especially Suze's complex and morally grey deal) and the main characters do NOT live perfectly, happily ever after, but good things do happen to them. Nell ends up such a cool woman after starting out like death, and I cheered her transformation the whole way. The hero has his flaws, but they are believable, everyday ones, no more twisted than anyone else's. Not like, "My father never thought I was good enough to be a real Lord Blackraven, so I pretended to be a horrible person! Even though I am totally not and we shall now live happily ever after!" Yes, there is a bit of an over-the-top fetishization of noir stuff in here, and yes, I did have a teensy bit of a problem with the secretary-boss dynamic and arguing that this relationship was somehow different than all those other secretary-boss relationships. But Crusie acknowledges the problems with that and works through it. <br /><br />It made me smile, it made me laugh, and it made me go, "hell yes!" when a few awesome things happened. This is a novel about two recognizable people getting through each day of life who get together and have a relationship. That sounds like it should be the whole romance novel genre, but sadly most incarnations I read are really about social status or going quietly mad. This is about a romance. I really appreciated that.<br /><br />ALERT: A ROMANCE NOVEL EXISTS. <br /><br />This has been a public service announcement. We will now return to your regularly scheduled programming.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="12199910453251991719">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer13163661286716642096">I thought that a lot of Min's obsessing came across as realistic, even if slightly too much. I think that's the way our deepest insecurities are. My o</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText13163661286716642096">I thought that a lot of Min's obsessing came across as realistic, even if slightly too much. I think that's the way our deepest insecurities are. My only problem with the book was I thought that the depiction of food as an aphrodisiac got a little disturbing as it got more and more emphasized throughout the book until the, er, climax. I also wish that Crusie didn't need to emphasize that "food is good!" so hard too because it started to get a little 'lady doth protest too much'. Other than that though I found the book funny and engaging, and I loved the female friendships depicted. <br /><br />This book was published in 2000, so it is definitely in the good range. Thanks for the tip, I'll try to stay with her older ones.</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_25111197">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/25111197" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/237469-miriam" class="left imgcol" title="Miriam"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1275489063p2/237469.jpg" alt="Miriam" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/25111197?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Mar 15, 2013</a>

      <a href="/user/show/237469-miriam" class="user" title="Miriam">Miriam</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/33728.Fast_Women" title="Paperback 9780312932794" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/237469-miriam?shelf=mystery" class="actionLinkLite">mystery</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer25111197">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9167334127399272143"><br />OK, they're not really <strong>fast</strong> exactly, but c'mon, they only have fragile little stumpy china legs. <br /><br /><img class="escapedImg" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380312707i/688686.jpg" /><br /><br />The Walking Ware may be only a metaphor (a pretty obvious one), but these women are Special Olympics fast, not Florence Griffith Joyner fast. They are like people who come out of comas and must slowly learn to walk again. Only, most of them seem to have never known how in the first place. <br /><br />Suze seemed in some ways to have the most excuse for her retardation: she married an older man whom she met while</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText9167334127399272143"><br />OK, they're not really <strong>fast</strong> exactly, but c'mon, they only have fragile little stumpy china legs. <br /><br /><img class="escapedImg" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380312707i/688686.jpg" /><br /><br />The Walking Ware may be only a metaphor (a pretty obvious one), but these women are Special Olympics fast, not Florence Griffith Joyner fast. They are like people who come out of comas and must slowly learn to walk again. Only, most of them seem to have never known how in the first place. <br /><br />Suze seemed in some ways to have the most excuse for her retardation: she married an older man whom she met while still in high school, and has never had to make a decision, must less work, and therefore has never developed interests or identity outside her marriage. It's understandable therefore, that she has a hard time admitting even to herself that her marriage is stifling; instead, her desire for escape and growth manifests itself in her obsession with “Walking Ware,” china with running feet. When her friend introduces her to the Walking Ware, “Suze lined up the running egg cups in a line and laughed. There were nine of them…all running hell bent for leather for someplace else.” She imagines the cups “running amok among the Spode,” the grimly painted heirloom china she is forced by her husband’s family to use, of which she says “I get very depressed looking at my china.” Having decided to buy some egg cups of her own, Suze “felt immeasurably lighter. She was going to have to get a job now. She had a future that didn’t involve going to school and waiting for Jack to get home. She was doing something.” At this point Suze has just begun to admit her own discontent with her sheltered life and has not yet realized that her husband is one of the things she is unhappy with.<br /><br />Nell, the main character, is pretending to be amicably divorced by denying even to herself that her husband cheated on her after using her for years to support and build his career. Now that his business is successful, he has traded her in for a younger and more attractive model. Although Nell is not to blame for the divorce, her sorrow reads more like a combination of bruised ego, financial anxiety, betrayal, and loss of stability than the rending heartbreak of having lost a deeply loved spouse. Her personal grief at the <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span style="display: none" class="spoilerContainer">[destruction of her china collection <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> seems more wrenching. But she really liked that stuff; her marriage seemed more of a purely practical investment.<br /><br />Crusie’s implicit criticism of the financial aspects of marriage is reminiscent of sociologist and philosopher Erich Fromm’s (whom Crusie cites in her critical writing) indictment of the objectifying view of love which approaches it as the purchase of best possible commodity (i.e. getting the most wealthy, prestigious, or attractive partner available given one’s own “exchange value” of attributes). Fromm argues that many people mistakenly conceive of love as being an easy, emotional reaction or a matter of sexual or material desire: “What most people in our culture mean by being lovable is essentially a mixture between being popular and having sex appeal.”<br /><br />This is a theme addressed in many of Crusie's novels -- the temptation or pressure to let relationship choices be guided by financial advantage, social or familiar pressures, or other non-emotional factors. Like Fromm, who asks and answers, “What does one person give another? He gives of himself…of his joy, of his interest, of his understanding, of his knowledge, of his humor, of sadness… In thus giving of his life, he enriches the other person,” Crusie urges readers to instead conceive of love as a process of mutual understanding and giving, to which honesty -- most of all with oneself -- is indispensable. <!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="9167334127399272143">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<span id="freeTextContainer5331629792291064493"><br /><strong>3 Stars! Too much going on and it was hard to keep track of, at least for me.</strong><br /><br />Usually this author's writing works for me, but unfortunately this won't go on my favorite read shelf. That's not to say it wasn't amusing and somewhat entertaining, but in the end, there were too many side stories that got in the way of the original plot, and I didn't enjoy it the way I wanted too. <br /><br /><strong>On the plus side</strong>, the narrator Sandra Burr was a pleasure to listen to. <br /><br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer6658539958122847665">Not my first Cruisie book , but I believe it will be my last. I have heard good things about this author and have tried to read her. First off, I liked the fact the characters were not 20 somethings, formula, etc. I liked that Nell was attempting to move on past the bumps in the road that life had dealt her. I have no clue what purpose her best friends served. They were all three annoying ,tiresome women. Who would get a job they apparently need and set out to antagonize the boss? I can see clea</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText6658539958122847665">Not my first Cruisie book , but I believe it will be my last. I have heard good things about this author and have tried to read her. First off, I liked the fact the characters were not 20 somethings, formula, etc. I liked that Nell was attempting to move on past the bumps in the road that life had dealt her. I have no clue what purpose her best friends served. They were all three annoying ,tiresome women. Who would get a job they apparently need and set out to antagonize the boss? I can see cleaning the office but the lengths she goes to, go beyond slapstick to stupid. Why does she disregard his feelings and opinions about HIS business? These women should have been named Ditz, Delirious and Dimwit! Nell's antics may have been intended to be humerous, but are not. If these women were real I would not want to know them. She deserved to be ditched by her husband and he made a wise choice. I felt sorry for the men, particularly Gabe and Riley. Why would women have sex within their own circle then disregard that and move on to next person within that same circle who just happens to be related to the first person. And what the heck was that lesbian encounter about. Arrrrrggg. These women are not lesbians so why even add that. And if they are why are the men EVEN IN THIS BOOK??? It makes no sense. One suggests they "tryst" while eating lasagna and ice cream. Why? No clue.... I'm done with Jennifer Cruisie. She disappoints.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1105076471">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer142442770376454676">I had reservations when my mom told me this book was funny because she likes a lot of books that I end up finding corny. Or worse, funny because they're trying too hard. But in this case, my mom was right. This book is hilarious. I don't often laugh-out-loud while reading, but I did more than a few times while reading this. The female protagonist, Nell, can be a little hard to connect with at times, and this is written for a generation of women ahead of my own, but even with that, I found I was</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText142442770376454676">I had reservations when my mom told me this book was funny because she likes a lot of books that I end up finding corny. Or worse, funny because they're trying too hard. But in this case, my mom was right. This book is hilarious. I don't often laugh-out-loud while reading, but I did more than a few times while reading this. The female protagonist, Nell, can be a little hard to connect with at times, and this is written for a generation of women ahead of my own, but even with that, I found I was able to connect with them and, even though I didn't necessarily agree with their choices, I understood why those decisions were made. The hero, Gabe, is just the right mix of charm, obliviousness, and stubborn insanity that I was able to like him despite himself, and the supporting cast was great. My favorite character was Margie. </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer18217423499192862072"><strong>3.5 Stars</strong><br /><br />This novel is quirky and hilarious! The writing style is good overall, but I did<br />get confused at times by some of the dialogue - loss of 1/2 star. Gotta love those Dysart women!<br /><br />Nell Dysart is sleepwalking through her life as a divorced woman. She didn't see it coming. And now she needs a job. She sits in Gabe McKenna's office at his detective agency and thinks of ways to fix it, all the while she is breaking a window, his chair arm, and poking a hole in his Oriental rug. McKenna hires Ne</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText18217423499192862072"><strong>3.5 Stars</strong><br /><br />This novel is quirky and hilarious! The writing style is good overall, but I did<br />get confused at times by some of the dialogue - loss of 1/2 star. Gotta love those Dysart women!<br /><br />Nell Dysart is sleepwalking through her life as a divorced woman. She didn't see it coming. And now she needs a job. She sits in Gabe McKenna's office at his detective agency and thinks of ways to fix it, all the while she is breaking a window, his chair arm, and poking a hole in his Oriental rug. McKenna hires Nell as favor to one of his biggest clients - Nell's former brother in law much to his chagrin. They are both kissers, strong alpha types, and are attracted to each other. Gabe has just been dumped by his ex-wife yet again. His partner and cousin, Riley, is tired of doing decoy jobs and has a hard on against Nell's best friend, Suze. Margie Dysart is another whole lot of crazy. All 3 women are some how connected to the O and D blackmail case and possibly a 20 year old death. <br /><br />When Nell gets to work on the office and the partners, O and D instructs the cousins to stop their investigation. They don't and the murders begin. And love is in the air, dog nabbing, arson, and everything else you can imagine. </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer10544633741349552166">*****MINOR SPOILERS!!!********<br /><br />1. Was anyone else REALLY disturbed about a 40 year old men having sex with an 18 year old high school student in a motel? And people looking at that photo and talking about how "in prime" Jack looked and NOT how it was a few months away from being statutory rape?<br /><br />2.   <span style="display:none" id="freeText10544633741349552166">*****MINOR SPOILERS!!!********<br /><br />1. Was anyone else REALLY disturbed about a 40 year old men having sex with an 18 year old high school student in a motel? And people looking at that photo and talking about how "in prime" Jack looked and NOT how it was a few months away from being statutory rape?<br /><br />2. OMG that whole convo about Gale understanding why men HIT THEIR WOMEN? Are you F-ing kidding me? Um, men don't hit women because "they love them so much they can't have them leave, but they can't stay with them either" - it's because they are abusive assholes who get off on attacking women who are physically and emotionally damaged. <br /><br />3. How ridiculous was it that Sus gave Tim a whole speech about infidelity and lack of loyalty...when she herself was a mistress. Usually, this is the part where people suddenly realize their own hypocrisy, but she just...didn't. <br /><br />4. I didn't think that Nell and Gabe had any type of real romantic connection or chemistry before they started having sex. The minor characters all randomly realized they were destined for each other, without any type of real reason. I was sort of rooting for Nell and Riley. <br /><br />5. What was the point of Marg? And the whole China story?<br /><br />6. When Gabe says "I know somebody's gotta sleep with my daughter, and it might as well be you". Um, a 19 year old does not NEED to be having sex. <br /><br />7. The whole mystery and murder story just became too convoluted and crazy and hard to keep track of. Judging from a few of her other books, Cruise needs to stop with the whole attempt to include Law and Order-esque plot points. They suck. <br /><br /></span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_108772852">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/108772852" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/248667-christy" class="left imgcol" title="Christy"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1404508394p2/248667.jpg" alt="Christy" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/108772852?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jun 26, 2010</a>

      <a href="/user/show/248667-christy" class="user" title="Christy">Christy</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/33728.Fast_Women" title="Paperback 9780312932794" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/248667-christy?shelf=mysteries" class="actionLinkLite">mysteries</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/248667-christy?shelf=romance" class="actionLinkLite">romance</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/248667-christy?shelf=21st-century-american-lit" class="actionLinkLite">21st-century-american-lit</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer108772852">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1011446000629554595">I really enjoyed this book. I liked the central characters a lot, and it made me happy. There is humor in this book and an approach to love, romance, and marriage that is grown-up and realistic while still maintaining a sense of fun and optimism. This isn't the kind of romance novel where the leads spend the whole book trying to avoid having sex and then when they do it's just happily-ever-after. They have to work at their relationship. They have to negotiate with each other to get what they nee</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText1011446000629554595">I really enjoyed this book. I liked the central characters a lot, and it made me happy. There is humor in this book and an approach to love, romance, and marriage that is grown-up and realistic while still maintaining a sense of fun and optimism. This isn't the kind of romance novel where the leads spend the whole book trying to avoid having sex and then when they do it's just happily-ever-after. They have to work at their relationship. They have to negotiate with each other to get what they need, to avoid hurting the other person, and to learn from their past mistakes. They grow as people and will continue to grow after the book ends because that's just what people do and, as this book acknowledges, the best relationships, the ones that work and that last, leave space for that kind of growth.<br /><br />There is no rape in this book. There are no man-roots or honey-ovens. Sex isn't always tied to true love, but it isn't used as a punishment or a means of control, either. This is a sex-positive book. <br /><br />Finally, there are positive female relationships and meaningful male relationships. A huge part of the book, in fact, revolves around the central female characters' friendship. They support each other, joke with each other, and do far more than simply talk about men or sex. There is also at least one significant male friendship, one in which the men talk, at least sometimes, about things that are important to them personally and in which they defend each other against others who don't understand or who would hurt them. On both sides, this makes the characters more likeable and believable and shifts the focus away from fulfillment through a romantic or sexual relationship and toward a broader sense of what defines and fulfills an individual (not just sex, but work, family, friends, hobbies, pets, etc.).<br /><br />The only major complaint I have about this book is that I think the title gives the wrong impression of the kind of women Crusie is writing about. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="1011446000629554595">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <a href="/user/show/115473-siria" class="user" title="Siria">Siria</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/115473-siria?shelf=21st-century" class="actionLinkLite">21st-century</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/115473-siria?shelf=romance" class="actionLinkLite">romance</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer26092900">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11672800014479849515">I quite liked this one, as it was frothy and fun but still somehow realistic—Crusie is good at setting up relationships between both the main and the secondary romantic couples which don't rely on external forces to create angst and drama, but rather at showing how repeated patterns of behaviour can ruin relationships without any outside help. I also liked the fact that Crusie is always happy to show her female characters taking genuine pleasure in their food, but not in a neurotic way, and that</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText11672800014479849515">I quite liked this one, as it was frothy and fun but still somehow realistic—Crusie is good at setting up relationships between both the main and the secondary romantic couples which don't rely on external forces to create angst and drama, but rather at showing how repeated patterns of behaviour can ruin relationships without any outside help. I also liked the fact that Crusie is always happy to show her female characters taking genuine pleasure in their food, but not in a neurotic way, and that her heroine is into her forties. There was one thing which niggled at my subconscious, though, and which made my eyebrows rise when I realised what it was: one character with a walk-on part was African-American, and I think in all the Crusies that I've read so far, she's the first character who hasn't been white. Hrm. How much of that is a function of setting (I'm not from the US, but the impression I've gotten is that the Mid-West, where these books are set, is terribly white?), I wonder, and how much is, well, good old white obliviousness?</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_268779199">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/268779199" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/7438487-olga-godim" class="left imgcol" title="Olga Godim"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1442639299p2/7438487.jpg" alt="Olga Godim" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/268779199?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jun 17, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/7438487-olga-godim" class="user" title="Olga Godim">Olga Godim</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/33728.Fast_Women" title="Paperback 9780312932794" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/7438487-olga-godim?shelf=jennifer-crusie" class="actionLinkLite">jennifer-crusie</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer268779199">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3341834945519416897">I love this writer. I’ve read everything she published and I subscribe to <a rel="nofollow" href="http://www.arghink.com/">her blog</a>. This re-read (it was originally published in 2001) gave me enormous pleasure and induced several laughing fits.<br />The story starts with the protagonist, Nell, coming to a job interview. She is a divorcee, still reeling from her husband’s betrayal after their 22 years of marriage. Her interviewer and potential employer, Gabe, owns a PI agency and he needs an office manager. <blockquote> <em>He picked up her resume. “Why did you leav</em></blockquote></span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText3341834945519416897">I love this writer. I’ve read everything she published and I subscribe to <a rel="nofollow" href="http://www.arghink.com/">her blog</a>. This re-read (it was originally published in 2001) gave me enormous pleasure and induced several laughing fits.<br />The story starts with the protagonist, Nell, coming to a job interview. She is a divorcee, still reeling from her husband’s betrayal after their 22 years of marriage. Her interviewer and potential employer, Gabe, owns a PI agency and he needs an office manager. <blockquote>
  <em>He picked up her resume. “Why did you leave your last position?”<br />“My boss divorced me.”<br />“That would be a reason,” he said, and began to read. </em>
</blockquote> The traditional start to this romantic caper is a camouflage. The story unfolds like a crossroad, leading in several nontraditional directions at once, all interlinked by their inventive creator, Crusie. It’s a comedy, so funny at times I couldn’t read because I laughed too hard. It’s a thrilling mystery with a number of frozen corpses, hidden boxes, and mysterious villains. It’s a story of female friendship and collector china. And above all, it’s a love story: it explores how love starts, how it matures, and how it ends. <br />Both protagonists, Nell and Gabe, are strong, assertive people. As they go about their day-to-day business: managing office or investigating clients, they fall in love. But love is not enough for a successful union, not for them. A couple must learn to compromise, to respect each other and accept each other’s foibles. And they both are old enough to know it.<br />To the reader’s delight, the process of such learning for Nell and Gabe is crammed with distractions: an embezzling former employee, YA children and former spouses, old family secrets and friends with marital problems. <br />This marvelous romp of a novel is written beautifully. About 80% of the text is dialog, and Crusie is definitely a master of dialog. Her snappy and hilarious one-liners or involved and smart verbal expositions propel the plot forward so swiftly, the reader gets a moving sickness just by keeping up. The story twists and turns and whirls around, and the reader can’t close the book until she knows what’s behind the next bend. <br />The little quote above is just a small snippet of the writer’s clean and witty writing style. There were so many other quotes I wanted to include they wouldn’t fit in a regular size review. I ended up including none of them. Read the book instead. <br />One of the subplots concerns Nell’s friend Suze and her collection of Carlton Walking Ware egg cups. The concept was intriguing enough that I Googled it. Below are a few pictures of the walking egg cups – they are real, alright. Quirky too, just like the story. <br /><br /><img width="300" class="escapedImg" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1403046333i/10029273.jpg" /><br /><img width="200" class="escapedImg" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1403046333i/10029274.jpg" /><br /><img width="400" height="170" class="escapedImg" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1403046333i/10029275.jpg" /><br /><br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="3341834945519416897">...more</a>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <a href="/user/show/6100047-sundae" class="user" title="Sundae">Sundae</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="did not like it">did not like it</span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer221376333">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6675308211278791591">Horrible. I stopped reading half way through.<br /><br />I don't know, I'm guessing I"m not the target demographic for this type of book because I found it extremely hard to relate to any of the characters. Being in my twenties, my humanist side roared with indignation at how appalling all these women acted and behaved, not to mention, the stereotypical ways all the men were portrayed. They were all manipulative, dysfunctional, and stupid people trying to do the "right" thing but actually doing the WRONG th</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText6675308211278791591">Horrible. I stopped reading half way through.<br /><br />I don't know, I'm guessing I"m not the target demographic for this type of book because I found it extremely hard to relate to any of the characters. Being in my twenties, my humanist side roared with indignation at how appalling all these women acted and behaved, not to mention, the stereotypical ways all the men were portrayed. They were all manipulative, dysfunctional, and stupid people trying to do the "right" thing but actually doing the WRONG things all the time. Instant gratification is all they fucking cared about, having a dignified and deserved place IN someone else's life is all they cared about, but these women refused to do anything for themselves by themselves and instead expected everything to be handed to them equally. Insult to women everywhere.<br /><br />And who the heck talks about china that much? This is not the 60's where you worth is measured by the type of china you have in your cabinets. And Nell, what a horrible, manipulative person. You're a secretary and you want half of a business that someone else worked to build for 22 years and you think you deserve in seven months? it was horrible.<br /><br />Bad plotting and horrible themes aside, the book had many mistakes (missing words), wasn't written well, wasn't in the least bit funny, had too many useless characters and kept dragging. Ugh. bad taste in my mouth.<br /><br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="6675308211278791591">...more</a>

          </span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_56134610">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/56134610" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/973665-christina" class="left imgcol" title="Christina"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1333294350p2/973665.jpg" alt="Christina" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/56134610?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jun 01, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/973665-christina" class="user" title="Christina">Christina</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/33728.Fast_Women" title="Paperback 9780312932794" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/973665-christina?shelf=meh" class="actionLinkLite">meh</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer56134610">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17093163806640865960">I read Jennifer Crusie's "Bet Me" recently and just LOVED it. It is by far my favorite romance I've read in a long time. Maybe ever. I loved the characters, the crazy circumstances and the funny witty dialogue. <br /><br />So imagine my disappointment with this book. <br /><br />Nell Dysart is a control freak forty-something, too-thin divorcee looking for a fresh start. Gabe is a control freak forty-something divorcee looking to maintain the status quo of his detective agency. <br /><br />In theory this book could have been great.</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText17093163806640865960">I read Jennifer Crusie's "Bet Me" recently and just LOVED it. It is by far my favorite romance I've read in a long time. Maybe ever. I loved the characters, the crazy circumstances and the funny witty dialogue. <br /><br />So imagine my disappointment with this book. <br /><br />Nell Dysart is a control freak forty-something, too-thin divorcee looking for a fresh start. Gabe is a control freak forty-something divorcee looking to maintain the status quo of his detective agency. <br /><br />In theory this book could have been great. It was an interesting power struggle between two alpha characters. The book was also filled with love, deception, dog-napping, blackmail and hideous business cards. In reality the book was a bit of a confusing read. There are too many characters with the same last name and halfway through I had to get out a notepad and write down all the characters just to get a handle on what was going on. The relationships between everyone were not very clear and it made the plot dull because I couldn't keep up with all the peripheral characters and really I quit caring. I think the book was supposed to be slapstick funny but instead it wandered all over the place.<br /><br />I think I could have dealt with the plot if it weren't for the fact that I didn't see how the two main characters were ever going to find some sort of balance in their lives. As two controlling, pushy people, they aren't very good to each other and their happy ending was lukewarm for me. Also I didn't even see an attraction between them until halfway though the book. The whole first half was a setup for the plot at the end. Also, while Jennifer Crusie knows how to build sexual tension, the sex scenes were strangely tepid. She never writes overly detailed sex scenes but they are usually quite sexy regardless. Welcome To Temptation is a particularly good example of her ability to write heated love scenes that aren't graphic. <br /><br />So with this book, there are characters who don't seem terribly attracted to each other, who aren't nice to one another and who have tepid sex... well the book just didn't do much for me. <br /><br />Ultimately the tug of war over who was going to wear the pants in the relationship was never resolved and I envisioned these two people engaged in a constant fight, making them both insane. It would have been easier to digest if Nell had understood anything about compromise but for every battle she won, she just started a new battle, leaving Gabe no even ground. She was determined that she was always right and that everything should be her way or no way at all. I plain didn't like her. <br /><br />Also as a heroine, she wasn't very bright. She stole a guy's dog because his ex-wife walked into the detective agency and said that he verbally abuses it by yelling all the time. Nell never stops to consider that maybe, the woman might not be honest. So she sneaks out in the night and steals it after being expressly told that she could be undermining the agency she works for and that she should not do it. Only much later does she even consider the idea that the woman may not have been truthful and by then, she decided to keep the dog rather than return it. She's headstrong to the point of coming of lunacy. <br /><br />Not a great book. It had moments but overall I was underwhelmed. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="17093163806640865960">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <a href="/user/show/6732447-hannah" class="left imgcol" title="Hannah"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1402096500p2/6732447.jpg" alt="Hannah" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/283136569?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Mar 01, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/6732447-hannah" class="user" title="Hannah">Hannah</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/8651327-fast-women" title="Audio CD 9781441840721" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/6732447-hannah?shelf=contemporary" class="actionLinkLite">contemporary</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/6732447-hannah?shelf=romance" class="actionLinkLite">romance</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/6732447-hannah?shelf=audio" class="actionLinkLite">audio</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/6732447-hannah?shelf=read-2012" class="actionLinkLite">read-2012</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer283136569">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1741422246941790832">I'm giving this book four stars, not so much because I loved it, but because it had a strong emotional impact on me. <em>Fast Women</em> was not an easy book to read. It contained some heartrendingly-accurate descriptions of the pain, the anger, the self-doubt, and the exhausting circular thinking that attends the end of a marriage. Even though I was exasperated with almost every character in this novel at one point or another, I could identify with almost all of them because they were struggling with th</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText1741422246941790832">I'm giving this book four stars, not so much because I loved it, but because it had a strong emotional impact on me. <em>Fast Women</em> was not an easy book to read. It contained some heartrendingly-accurate descriptions of the pain, the anger, the self-doubt, and the exhausting circular thinking that attends the end of a marriage. Even though I was exasperated with almost every character in this novel at one point or another, I could identify with almost all of them because they were struggling with the same emotions and concepts that I've struggled with before in similar circumstances. <br /><br /><em>Fast Women</em> was a departure from the kinds of romance novels I've gravitated toward in the past. I usually prefer my happily-ever-afters a little bit tidier. This novel's ending, while very hopeful, didn't quite leave me with warm fuzzies. On the other hand, the character's emotions and dilemmas were so complex and so believable that I will probably remember this book long after I've forgotten some of the other more "satisfying" romances I've read.<br /></span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_551049155">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/551049155" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/13779-k" class="left imgcol" title="K"><img src="http://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" alt="K" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/551049155?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Mar 12, 2013</a>

      <a href="/user/show/13779-k" class="user" title="K">K</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/33728.Fast_Women" title="Paperback 9780312932794" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">women seeking bodice ripper wish fulfillment thinly disguised as chick lit mystery</span></div>

        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/13779-k?shelf=mysteriesthrillers" class="actionLinkLite">mysteriesthrillers</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/13779-k?shelf=marysues" class="actionLinkLite">marysues</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/13779-k?shelf=audiobooks" class="actionLinkLite">audiobooks</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/13779-k?shelf=should-ve-been-shorter" class="actionLinkLite">should-ve-been-shorter</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/13779-k?shelf=chicklit" class="actionLinkLite">chicklit</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer551049155">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer726659709247332812">Meh. I was really hoping for more.<br /><br />I was hoping this would be like a good <a title="Susan Isaacs" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/37244.Susan_Isaacs">Susan Isaacs</a> book, something along the lines of <a title="Long Time No See by Susan Isaacs" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/469847.Long_Time_No_See">Long Time No See</a> or <a title="After all these years by Susan Isaacs" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2275932.After_all_these_years">After all these years</a>. Meaning yes, a light read with some romance and a happy ending, but also a mystery and unconventional main characters I'd actually meet, or would want to meet, in real life. I think <a title="Jennifer Crusie" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/19005.Jennifer_Crusie">Jennifer Crusie</a> was trying for that effect and while I acknowledge some limited success, overall this book didn't make it for me.<br /><br />We meet Nell, a beaten-do</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText726659709247332812">Meh. I was really hoping for more.<br /><br />I was hoping this would be like a good <a title="Susan Isaacs" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/37244.Susan_Isaacs">Susan Isaacs</a> book, something along the lines of <a title="Long Time No See by Susan Isaacs" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/469847.Long_Time_No_See">Long Time No See</a> or <a title="After all these years by Susan Isaacs" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2275932.After_all_these_years">After all these years</a>. Meaning yes, a light read with some romance and a happy ending, but also a mystery and unconventional main characters I'd actually meet, or would want to meet, in real life. I think <a title="Jennifer Crusie" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/19005.Jennifer_Crusie">Jennifer Crusie</a> was trying for that effect and while I acknowledge some limited success, overall this book didn't make it for me.<br /><br />We meet Nell, a beaten-down fortyish divorcee, who is applying for a job with Gabe's detective agency. Gabe is also fortyish and conveniently unattached, and the minute any peripheral character acquainted with both Nell and Gabe hears about the interview, he or she immediately predicts that Nell and Gabe will end up together. How about hitting me over the head a little more with that foreshadowing, Crusie? I mean, this <em>is</em> a romance novel after all. How could they <em>not</em> end up together? But sure, put the prediction into another three characters' mouths why don't you.<br /><br />It does take a while for Nell and Gabe to end up together, which I guess was Crusie's attempt to avoid falling into total Harlequin territory. But once they do, that's it. The romance (and Nell and Gabe's intermittent catfighting which could only, of course, be solved by more romance) was straight out of any wish fulfillment drugstore novel. He's every woman's dream! And he thinks Nell is beautiful! As do lots of other guys, suddenly! (One of my pet peeves in these types of books -- the female author slipping into the male viewpoint only so she can put words into his mouth about how bowled over he is by the heroine). He's great! She's great! Even their fights are great! We can pretend they're not Mary Sues by giving them some charming quirks, but they're still Mary Sues.<br /><br />The mystery seemed silly and over-the-top to me, as did the ridiculous dognapping episode. As another goodreads reviewer said, Nell suffers from serious bouts of TSTL -- too stupid to live. Some of the dumb stuff she gets away with is just ridiculous. I also agree with some reviewers who pointed out that there's a serious retro quality to this book -- the women's lack of independence seemed a bit anachronistic, although unfortunately I do know people who struggle with these issues so I don't want to come down too hard on that point.<br /><br />I'm not such a snob that I can't enjoy a good chick lit novel. But for me, this was not a good chick lit novel. <br /><br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="726659709247332812">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer2660948545451280230"><u> <strong> <em>Fast Women</em> </strong> </u><br /><br /><strong> <em>The Characters</em> </strong><br /><br />Gabe <br />Nell <br /><br />And a bunch of other folks. <br /><br /><strong> <em>The Story</em> </strong><br /><br />This story was really interesting and really complicated. A who-done-it story laced with friendship, comedy and love. <br /><br /><br /><strong> <em>The Random Thoughts</em> </strong><br /><br />This story once again proves that I can not go wrong with a Jennifer Crusie book. But, now I’ve read all of the back catalogue and she needs to write me some new stuff. <br /><br /><strong>4 Stars</strong></span>
