<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_818647960">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/818647960" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/2257721-wendy" class="left imgcol" title="Wendy"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1388948080p2/2257721.jpg" alt="Wendy" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/818647960?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Apr 05, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/2257721-wendy" class="user" title="Wendy">Wendy</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/10859649-fast-women" title="Kindle Edition " class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer818647960">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8661859280443833514">One of my unofficial goals this year is to take part in more of the group reads in one of my online book groups, On the Porch Swing. The group often has interesting and lively discussions, and I wanted to be a part of that this year. To begin the year, January's pick was Fast Women by Jennifer Crusie. I have never read anything by this author before, although I have heard of her. She's a favorite in many circles.<br /><br />I did not really know what to expect when I began reading Fast Women. When I hear Je</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText8661859280443833514">One of my unofficial goals this year is to take part in more of the group reads in one of my online book groups, On the Porch Swing. The group often has interesting and lively discussions, and I wanted to be a part of that this year. To begin the year, January's pick was Fast Women by Jennifer Crusie. I have never read anything by this author before, although I have heard of her. She's a favorite in many circles.<br /><br />I did not really know what to expect when I began reading Fast Women. When I hear Jennifer Crusie's name, I automatically think romance, and in this book, there was plenty of that. The mystery, however, often takes center stage in the novel, which makes it more my kind of story.<br /><br />While Gabe and Nell are the main protagonists, there are other characters who have strong story lines throughout the novel, including Gabe's partner Riley and Nell's best friends (and sisters-in-law), Suze and Margie. <br /><br />Betrayal, loss, women coming into their own, redefining who they are later in life, and finding love after having been betrayed are themes that each of the women in the novel share. I really appreciated the depth the author went into in fleshing out her characters, even the more minor ones, and their motivations. The growth of the more major characters over the course of the novel was also well done, including the self reflection and re-assessment of their situations. By the end of the novel, it's easy to see why certain things happened the way they did, even if bad decisions were made. In terms of the relationships gone sour, I mean.<br /><br />In terms of the mystery, well, I liked how the author built up to the climax. It was a slow build, built around the characters and their personal drama, but the more events came to light, the more complex and slippery the mystery became. Like the relationships in this book, the mystery itself is one big tangle. Until its not. I appreciated the internal struggle Gabe was going through, concerned his father may have been involved in or had covered up the murder of the wife of his father's long time friend. It really would be difficult to be in that situation. Like Gabe, I would want to know the truth, to hope to clear my father's name. <br /><br />I liked the characters alright. I wanted to like them more. My first thought was that perhaps it has to do with the fact that I cannot really relate to what they are going through in their personal lives, dealing with marital affairs and divorce, but other authors have been able to draw me and help me relate without any trouble. So, it can't be that. I think part of it was the fact that so much was going on in the novel, as well as my just not really connecting with any of the characters. <br /><br />Even so, I really felt for Nell. She had worked hard her entire life, helping her husband establish his insurance business, basically running it for him, raising their son, and then all of that disappeared out from under her when her husband left her for another woman. It made me angry and sad. One of my favorite scenes in the novel is when Nell finally lets loose and lets her ex know how she really feels about his actions.<br /><br />Of the characters though, my favorite would have to be Gabe. He was a good person and there was nothing about him that was manipulative or shifty or dishonest. He could be clueless at times, but he admitted when he was wrong (mostly).<br /><br />One of the aspects of the novel I appreciated too was the juxtaposition of the young and the old(er). Although Nell's son and Gabe's daughter were not focused on often in the novel, they were enough of a presence to get a feel for the differences and similarities between new and more established romantic relationships.<br /><br />There is also the relationship between the women. Their friendship was quite strong and I thought it was wonderful how they supported each other, how they banded together when one of them needed help, whether it be stealing a dog or working through a divorce. I'm always a little envious of relationships like that. I don't really have any close women friends like that. While I liked Nell, I never warmed completely to Suze and I just felt sorry for Margie. Both women were dealing with their own issues. Suze was that other woman who had broken up a marriage, married the guy, and was now unhappy. Margie's husband disappeared fifteen years before and she was living with another man who wanted her to marry him, but Margie wasn't willing to commit.<br /><br />Fast Women is a wonderful book for a book discussion, which I hadn't expected when I first started reading it. I think many of us who have been married for many years can relate to how hard marriage can be sometimes, how many compromises we have to make in life in general once we have families, and how we change and evolve over time. <br /><br />For all the seriousness of the issues covered in this novel, what made it especially enjoyable for me was the humor. There were comical scenes and witty dialogue throughout. And you can't forget the mystery aspect: murder, secrets, and good china. <br /><br />I am glad I read this book. Had it not been for my book group, I would not have, and I would have missed out in a good book. Even despite it's flaws, I still liked it.</span>

      <a href="/user/show/3901425-jerry" class="user" title="Jerry">Jerry</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer112958647">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17567918091528250540"> Funny and witty, but a lot of characters to track...<br /><br />One of the (regular-speed) women in our book club selected an author new to us, Jennifer Crusie. We picked up "Fast Women" out of amusement with the title, although we're not really sure the book is aptly named. Early on, we almost confused leading lady Nell Dysart with Evanovich's Stephanie Plum - on a job interview, Nell breaks just about everything she touches in the prospective boss's office. But detective Gabe McKenna hires her anyway, an</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText17567918091528250540"> Funny and witty, but a lot of characters to track...<br /><br />One of the (regular-speed) women in our book club selected an author new to us, Jennifer Crusie. We picked up "Fast Women" out of amusement with the title, although we're not really sure the book is aptly named. Early on, we almost confused leading lady Nell Dysart with Evanovich's Stephanie Plum - on a job interview, Nell breaks just about everything she touches in the prospective boss's office. But detective Gabe McKenna hires her anyway, and we're off and running as Nell tries to put aside her divorce after 22 years of marriage. Girlfriends Suze (HOT!) and Margie (NOT!) add a lot of interesting dialogue and opinions to the early tale as they discuss all their men troubles and the outlook for Nell at the agency. Nell turns out to be super efficient as an office manager, which tends to upset Gabe's applecart as he likes things the old way. This tension delays what turns out to be a torrid romance between the two, but one that causes near the novel's end a fair degree of deliberation over just what a relationship and/or marriage needs as a true foundation.<br /><br />Along the way, a murder mystery helps move along a somewhat contrived plot, but funny situations are more the point than solving the old crime. Even a dog-napping adds interest to the story line. The numerous characters and marital status changes sometimes get confusing. Nell is pretty obsessive at times as well. But before it's over, things change for all the girlfriends and give us readers a lot to chew on.<br /><br />A light read for sure, but Crusie manages to squeeze in a lot of humor, just the right amount of romance and sex (some casual), and a thought-provoking ending that by and large will please. <br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="17567918091528250540">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <a href="/user/show/6986051-janel" class="user" title="Janel">Janel</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer351350808">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6959864662509517807">If you want to be happy and entertained you can't go wrong with a Jennifer Crusie novel. This one was filled with offbeat characters, snappy dialog, some sexy scenes here and there, and peppered throughout with a little wisdom and a lot of humor. Fast Women is set to the backdrop of a detective agency and has a decidedly 1940's vibe in a very modern story. There's lots of good chemistry between the characters, and an underlying question or theme regarding the pros and cons of marriage. Some of i</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText6959864662509517807">If you want to be happy and entertained you can't go wrong with a Jennifer Crusie novel. This one was filled with offbeat characters, snappy dialog, some sexy scenes here and there, and peppered throughout with a little wisdom and a lot of humor. Fast Women is set to the backdrop of a detective agency and has a decidedly 1940's vibe in a very modern story. There's lots of good chemistry between the characters, and an underlying question or theme regarding the pros and cons of marriage. Some of it gets a little silly sometimes, such as the dog napping storyline, but I just went with it and accepted it as part of the fun. Sometimes I got irritated at how stubborn some of the characters were, and got confused once in while with the murder mystery that ties the story together, but really these issues were minor. I liked the symbolism of the meanings of the china patterns the women collected and really want to go on ebay and buy a piece of vintage "walking ware" now. A great beach or backyard on the lounge chair read this summer. Lots of fun!</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="6959864662509517807">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer1990493094716210687">I've purchased this book on audio 3 times! The two occasions something has been wrong with the cassettes. I even wrote to the company and they helpfully sent me a new broken cassette. So for the third try, I moved into the digital age and downloaded it from audible.com. I really do like Jennifer Crusie and the what I'd heard of the book so far convinced me I wasn't going to be wasting my money (again). <br /><br />I didn't waste my money or my time. <em>Fast Women</em> is a fun and entertaining "read". It has really</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText1990493094716210687">I've purchased this book on audio 3 times! The two occasions something has been wrong with the cassettes. I even wrote to the company and they helpfully sent me a new broken cassette. So for the third try, I moved into the digital age and downloaded it from audible.com. I really do like Jennifer Crusie and the what I'd heard of the book so far convinced me I wasn't going to be wasting my money (again). <br /><br />I didn't waste my money or my time. <em>Fast Women</em> is a fun and entertaining "read". It has really great motifs -- mad-cap comedy (stealing the dog), nods to noir (two modern detectives stuck in there 50's office), and zany smart women who are very funny and insightful (about other if not themselves). I like Jennifer Crusie because she makes me laugh. I like her because she tells a slightly unconventional romance. I like her writing because her characters seem real in all their outlandish imperfection. This was a good book and the only reason it has four stars instead of five is because <em>Faking It</em>, also by Crusie, is a tough act to beat. <br /></span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer379719288">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6774552346404180781">This book was a humorous romantic mystery. This is not a laugh-out-loud book, but you do find yourself giggling in quit a few places. Be warned, there is sex, but not too graphic, and the "f" word is used every once in a while. This is not a Christian book, it is secular, so the hero/heroine drink and have sex outside of marriage. That, however, is the world we live in. <br /><br />I had most of the mystery figured out well before the end, but with all the antics of the heroine and her friends, I found myse</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText6774552346404180781">This book was a humorous romantic mystery. This is not a laugh-out-loud book, but you do find yourself giggling in quit a few places. Be warned, there is sex, but not too graphic, and the "f" word is used every once in a while. This is not a Christian book, it is secular, so the hero/heroine drink and have sex outside of marriage. That, however, is the world we live in. <br /><br />I had most of the mystery figured out well before the end, but with all the antics of the heroine and her friends, I found myself wanting to read further. I almost wish Ms. Crusie had left off the romance part and just focused on the three women. I think it would have made for a more interesting story.<br /><br />However, over all, it was a good read. Ms. Crusie places your directly in the scene with wonderful description. Her dialogue seems to be spot on between the hero and heroine, though at times I felt it forced with some of the other characters. <br /><br />But if you want a fun quick read, take a chance on this one. I think you'll find yourself snickering as you go along. </span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_135265276">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/135265276" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/754607-nan" class="left imgcol" title="Nan"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1277820071p2/754607.jpg" alt="Nan" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer135265276">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15130558256032481078">I stopped in at the County library today, looking for a fix. I wanted something light and funny. I walked out with three Jennifer Crusie novels that I'd never read, and I finished this one within a few hours. It was exactly what I wanted.<br /><br />As the cover copy explains, Nell and Gabe are both divorced. Nell's been in a bad place since her divorce; she's depressed, and she doesn't even have the desire to eat. Her friend, Suze, tells her that Gabe needs a secretary, and since Nell finally reaches the s</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText15130558256032481078">I stopped in at the County library today, looking for a fix. I wanted something light and funny. I walked out with three Jennifer Crusie novels that I'd never read, and I finished this one within a few hours. It was exactly what I wanted.<br /><br />As the cover copy explains, Nell and Gabe are both divorced. Nell's been in a bad place since her divorce; she's depressed, and she doesn't even have the desire to eat. Her friend, Suze, tells her that Gabe needs a secretary, and since Nell finally reaches the stage where she wants to move forward, she goes to the interview.<br /><br />Gabe has been divorced for years. His ex-wife was smarter than him a number of ways; she'd realized that no matter how much they loved each other, they were not each other's soul mates. Their divorce doesn't put much of a crimp in their sexual relationship. However, Chloe, his sort-of-ex, decides its finally time to end things. She needs to take her life forward, and she can't do that if she stays with Gabe where it's comfortable.<br /><br />Alone, looking for new lives, Gabe and Nell are drawn to one another, but at the same time leary of this attraction they feel. Having been burned before, they're both scared to take their relationship outside of work, to invest in each other emotionally. </span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_568321762">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/568321762" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/14706534-lg-a-library-girl-s-familiar-diversions" class="left imgcol" title="LG (A Library Girl's Familiar Diversions)"><img src="http://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" alt="LG (A Library Girl's Familiar Diversions)" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/568321762?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Mar 22, 2013</a>

      <a href="/user/show/14706534-lg-a-library-girl-s-familiar-diversions" class="user" title="LG (A Library Girl's Familiar Diversions)">LG (A Library Girl's Familiar Diversions)</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="did not like it">did not like it</span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/33728.Fast_Women" title="Paperback 9780312932794" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/14706534-lg-a-library-girl-s-familiar-diversions?shelf=1-star" class="actionLinkLite">1-star</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/14706534-lg-a-library-girl-s-familiar-diversions?shelf=read-2008" class="actionLinkLite">read-2008</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/14706534-lg-a-library-girl-s-familiar-diversions?shelf=format-print" class="actionLinkLite">format-print</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/14706534-lg-a-library-girl-s-familiar-diversions?shelf=acquired-library" class="actionLinkLite">acquired-library</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer568321762">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer516772544117912132">After Nell Dysart divorced her husband of 22 years, she lost her appetite for everything. Because her friends, Suze and Margie, are worried about her, she gets a job as a secretary at Gabe McKenna's detective agency. Of course, Gabe's biggest clients are also all the men who are or once were in Nell and her friends lives, so it's not like she's getting too fresh a start. Gabe's agency starts looking into a blackmail case involving those men, and things start getting very complicated.<br /><br />This makes i</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText516772544117912132">After Nell Dysart divorced her husband of 22 years, she lost her appetite for everything. Because her friends, Suze and Margie, are worried about her, she gets a job as a secretary at Gabe McKenna's detective agency. Of course, Gabe's biggest clients are also all the men who are or once were in Nell and her friends lives, so it's not like she's getting too fresh a start. Gabe's agency starts looking into a blackmail case involving those men, and things start getting very complicated.<br /><br />This makes it sound like the book is mostly about Nell and Gabe, but it's not. There's Riley, Gabe's partner in the agency, who's been pining over Suze for years. Of course, she doesn't even know he exists, and she's married. Things start getting rocky with her husband (Jack) because he wants her to stay home and look pretty and not go out, get a job, and have a life that doesn't involve him in every aspect - by the way, Suze was once "the other woman" when Jack was married to his second wife. Then there's Margie, who's dating a guy named Budge. Margie drinks a lot because Budge wants her to marry him and that's not what she wants to do. Technically, she's still married to her husband, who left years ago and may be dead, but if she declares him dead then she won't have a convenient excuse for turning down Budge. Also, back to Nell and Gabe, it's not like things are going perfectly for them either. Nell and Gabe fight a lot (and have a lot of make-up sex, but that's not the point) because they're both stubborn as hell. Gabe doesn't want any changes in his life and his agency, and Nell wants to redo everything at the agency and sees any sort of giving in as allowing him to use her as a doormat. Remember, however, that Nell is the secretary, and really, truly should be getting Gabe's approval and input before changing things and replacing furniture instead of railroading over him.<br /><br />Granted, I haven't read many Jennifer Crusie books (I think this is my fifth one), but I'm used to her books being funny, romantic, and frequently heart-tugging and exasperating at the same time. I'm not used to her characters being annoying, rigid, and generally unlikeable, which is how I viewed the characters in this book most of the time. Basically, Riley came off as the most emotionally healthy character, and he was the one dealing with his feelings for Suze by dating/sleeping with anything female (like an undergrad, or Nell). Gabe's resistance to change was understandable, at first, but it got really annoying when he continued to resist even the changes that made sense. Nell acted like a bulldozer in Gabe's agency, and (because of her divorce) she was left with the impression that giving in a little is the same as letting yourself get walked on. Suze is a doormat who thinks she needs a man in her life in order to be complete, and she feels this so wholeheartedly that she's willing to give up having a life of her own in order to have a man around. At first I thought Margie was a bimbo, but it turns out that she was just a perpetual drunk with no tact.<br /><br />None of these characters started to feel like people I'd actually want to get to know until maybe 50 pages before the ending of this 400+ page book. This wasn't the enjoyable, relaxing reading experience I was expecting when I plucked a book with "Crusie" on the cover off of a public library bookshelf. In her dedication, Crusie wrote "For Valerie Taylor, because she tells me when my scenes are boring, my syntax is twisted, and my characters are jerks..." Apparently, Ms. Taylor had her work cut out for her if this is the characters after they were made to be less like jerks, and maybe she should have also been working on telling Crusie to make her characters less like wet washcloths.<br /><br />I don't think romance novel couples have to be perfect and have perfect relationships in order for them to be fun to read about. I do like for there to be something pleasant about their relationships, though. In addition, it probably didn't help (for me, anyway) that all or most of the characters were older than the usual romance novel age, which means they were old enough to be my parents. For example, I think Nell's son was a little over 20.<br /><br />So, if I disliked the book this much, why did I keep reading it?<br />- Jennifer Crusie wrote it, so I was hoping it would get better.<br />- Some of the information about china that Suze, Nell, and Margie were talking about sounded interesting, even if I think Crusie could've edited those bits down more. The Walking Ware and Running Ware sounded like fun, though.<br />- Marlene, the dachshund, was interesting. My family has a dachshund, and, even though he doesn't flirt and act abused for biscuits, he does flirt for belly rubs.<br /><br /><strong>(Original review posted on <a rel="nofollow" href="http://familiardiversions.blogspot.com/2008/05/fast-women-by-jennifer-crusie.html">A Library Girl's Familiar Diversions</a>.)</strong></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="516772544117912132">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

Crusie does unresolved sexual tension very well, with a good line in resolving it too. There's a complicated murder investigation going on in the background, which I <em>think</em>I followed.   <span style="display:none" id="freeText1801390200471743597"><div>The first half of this shapes up really well - The Maltese Falcon on speed.  Crusie does unresolved sexual tension very well, with a good line in resolving it too.  There's a complicated murder investigation going on in the background, which I <em>think</em> I followed.  Points deducted for the fact that too much time is spent on secondary characters at the expense of the MCs' story, and for some strange conflicts introduced into the MC story at the end.  Less is more, sometimes.  But - it's Crusie and so worth the read.</div></span>

      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;name=' + shelf_name + '&amp;a=' + action + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('PcwwWVSb6gvAX0tzixUCMvcyw2BsfAI97n7s/SIwlvtYGA+Kpkn+8UyHP8j1dOSAvsUAeSWhRZeEd+lv7qVgvg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&amp;book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;refresh=true' + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('jQ/sBfcs1MA5UFhJ3nVecn8lbuxIUk4M/YKXzh9usDzo29PWBf7AOrWILPKgFLjANtKt9QGPCaaXi5Jc0/tGeQ==')})
  }
//]]&gt;
</script>

    <div class=" clearFloats bigBox" id="aboutAuthor"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/19005.Jennifer_Crusie">About Jennifer Crusie</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
      <a href="/author/show/19005.Jennifer_Crusie"><img alt="19005" src="http://d.gr-assets.com/authors/1295982567p2/19005.jpg" class="right" /></a>
    <div class="readable">
      
<span id="freeTextContainer12412241788990336952">Jenny Crusie is the NYT bestselling author of twenty some novels and lots of other stuff. Her latest novel, Maybe This Time, hit shelves in August, 2010.<br /><br />Jenny lives on the Ohio River where she often stares at the ceiling and counts her blessings.</span>
